class="container td-page-wrap"> <div class="row"> <div class="span12"> <div class="td-grid-wrap"> <div class="container-fluid"> <div class="row-fluid "> <div class="span8 column_container" role="main" itemprop="mainContentOfPage" itemscope="itemscope" itemtype="http://schema.org/Blog"> <article id="post-19381" class="post-19381 post type-post status-publish format-video has-post-thumbnail hentry category-featured category-politics category-us tag-julia-pierson tag-nashville-police tag-police-chief-steve-anderson tag-president-obama tag-secret-service" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Article"> <header> <h1 itemprop="name" class="entry-title">Oath Upheld: Nashville Cops Refused Secret Service Request for Illegal Search of Obama Critic</h1> <div class="meta-info"> <ul class="td-category"><li class="entry-category"><a href="http://benswann.com/category/politics/">Politics</a></li><li class="entry-category"><a href="http://benswann.com/category/politics/us/">US</a></li></ul>By: <b>Barry Donegan</b> <time itemprop="dateCreated" class="entry-date updated" datetime="2014-10-15T18:38:44+00:00">Oct 15, 2014</time><meta itemprop="interactionCount" content="UserComments:334"/> <div class="entry-comments-views"><span class="td-sp td-sp-ico-comments td-fake-click" data-fake-click="http://benswann.com/oath-upheld-nashville-cops-refused-secret-service-request-for-illegal-search-of-obama-critic/#comments"></span>334</div> </div> </header> <p class="td-sub-title">Nashville Police Chief Steve Anderson recently sent a letter to Congress alleging that Secret Service agents asked Nashville police to falsify a warrant so that the agents could search the home of a Nashville resident who had posted about President Obama on Facebook. </p> <div class="wpb_video_wrapper"> <iframe width="600" height="560" src="http://www.youtube.com/embed/Qt0CIUqljsI?feature=oembed&wmode=opaque" frameborder="0" allowfullscreen=""></iframe> </div> <div class="mr_social_sharing_wrapper">  <span class="mr_social_sharing"><fb:share-button type="button_count" href="http://benswann.com/oath-upheld-nashville-cops-refused-secret-service-request-for-illegal-search-of-obama-critic/"></fb:share-button></span><span class="mr_social_sharing"><div class="g-plusone" data-size="medium" data-href="http://benswann.com/oath-upheld-nashville-cops-refused-secret-service-request-for-illegal-search-of-obama-critic/"></div></span><span class="mr_social_sharing"><a href="http://www.stumbleupon.com/submit?url=http%3A%2F%2Fbenswann.com%2Foath-upheld-nashville-cops-refused-secret-service-request-for-illegal-search-of-obama-critic%2F" class="mr_social_sharing_popup_link"><img src="http://benswann.com/wp-content/plugins/social-sharing-toolkit/images/buttons/stumbleupon.png" class="nopin" alt="Submit to StumbleUpon" title="Submit to StumbleUpon"/></a></span><span class="mr_social_sharing"><a href="https://twitter.com/share" class="twitter-share-button" data-count="horizontal" data-url="http://benswann.com/oath-upheld-nashville-cops-refused-secret-service-request-for-illegal-search-of-obama-critic/" data-via="BenSwann_" data-text="Oath Upheld: Nashville Cops Refused Secret Service Request for Illegal Search of Obama Critic"></a></span><span class="mr_social_sharing"><a class="linksalpha_button linksalpha_link" href="//www.linksalpha.com/social/mobile" data-url="http://benswann.com/oath-upheld-nashville-cops-refused-secret-service-request-for-illegal-search-of-obama-critic/" data-text="Oath Upheld: Nashville Cops Refused Secret Service Request for Illegal Search of Obama Critic" data-desc="Following Secret Service Director Julia Pierson's recent resignation over a major security breach at the White House, new allegations are facing the president's embattled security detail. According to Phil Williams at News Channel 5, Nashville Police Chief Steve Anderson sent a scathing letter last" data-image="http://benswann.com/wp-content/uploads/2014/10/maxresdefault10-232x150.jpg" data-button="none"> <img src="//www.linksalpha.com/images/social_share_button.png" alt="Share" class="linksalpha_image"/> </a><script type="text/javascript" src="//www.linksalpha.com/scripts/loader_iconbox.js?v=2.3"></script></span></div><p>Following Secret Service Director Julia Pierson&#8217;s <a title="Time on Julia Pierson's Resignation" href="http://time.com/3453528/secret-service-julie-pierson-resign/" target="_blank">recent resignation</a> over a major security breach at the White House, new allegations are facing the president&#8217;s embattled security detail. According to Phil Williams at <a title="News Channel 5 on Secret Service Scandal" href="http://www.jrn.com/newschannel5/news/newschannel-5-investigates/Police-Chief-Accuses-Secret-Service-Of-Misconduct-279207151.html" target="_blank"><em>News Channel 5</em></a>, Nashville Police Chief Steve Anderson sent a <a title="Nashville's Chief Anderson's Letter to Congress" href="https://www.documentcloud.org/documents/1312810-steve-anderson-letter-regarding-secret-service.html" target="_blank">scathing letter</a> last week to the House Committee on Oversight complaining that Secret Service agents asked Nashville police officers to <a title="Nashville Scene on the Secret Service Scandal" href="http://www.nashvillescene.com/pitw/archives/2014/10/15/report-secret-service-asked-metro-cops-to-fake-a-warrant" target="_blank">falsify a warrant</a> during an investigation into a local resident who allegedly posted &#8220;threatening&#8221; comments about President Obama on Facebook.</p> <p>Williams&#8217; report notes that, in January of 2013, Secret Service agents working out of the Nashville field office visited the home of the resident who made the Facebook postings and knocked on his door. Then, an agent called local police and asked for backup, stating that the individual was refusing to let them in without a warrant and appeared to be armed. When Nashville police arrived, they informed the Secret Service agents that the man in question is a licensed gun owner, did not violate the law, and that a warrant would be required in order to investigate further. Chief Anderson said in his letter, &#8220;one of the agents then asked a [Nashville police] sergeant to &#8216;wave a piece of paper&#8217; in an apparent effort to dupe the resident into thinking that they indeed had a warrant.&#8221; Faced with a request to violate their oath of office and the rights of a citizen, the officers with the Metro Nashville Police Department flatly refused and left the scene.</p><div class="wpInsert wpInsertInPostAd wpInsertMiddle" style="margin: 5px; padding: 0px;"><center>   <div id='div-gpt-ad-1413662029612-0' style='width:300px; height:250px;'> <script type='text/javascript'> googletag.cmd.push(function() { googletag.display('div-gpt-ad-1413662029612-0'); }); </script> </div> <br></center></div> <p>Chief Anderson, upset that his officers were asked to violate a citizen&#8217;s rights in a way that could have escalated into a dangerous situation, contacted then Secret Service Director Julia Pierson and Assistant Director A.T. Smith to file a complaint. Pierson did not reply to Anderson, but Smith did so in a demeaning tone, essentially telling Nashville&#8217;s police chief to &#8220;mind [his] own affairs&#8221; and refusing to investigate the incident.</p> <p>An angry Anderson then met with officials in the Secret Service&#8217;s Nashville field office and asked, &#8220;Do you think it is appropriate to wave a piece of paper in the air and tell him you have a warrant when you do not have a warrant?&#8221; In his letter, Anderson noted that an unnamed Secret Service official replied, &#8220;I don&#8217;t know. I&#8217;m not a lawyer.&#8221; Anderson then inquired as to why Secret Service agents would request that Nashville police falsify a warrant if they felt that it was something that they had lawful authority to do, implying that merely by asking, the agents were demonstrating their understanding that they were making an illegal request. Anderson noted that his &#8220;complaint was not well-received&#8221; and that officials would not offer any reassurance that similar incidents would be prevented in the future.</p> <p>Chief Anderson believes that the Nashville incident is evidence that corruption in the Secret Service runs deeper than just its director. He feels that there are problems with the culture of the organization and that major administrative reform is necessary. As the above-embedded video by <em>News Channel 5</em> points out, Anderson indicated that, in the future, Nashville police officers will have to request permission from top officials before assisting Secret Service agents in further investigations.</p> <p>As a side note, back in May of 2013, shortly after the incident, Secret Service agents <a title="WKRN on Michelle Obama's Visit" href="http://www.wkrn.com/story/22251605/metro-police-wont-provide-security-for-first-ladys-upcoming-visit" target="_blank">did not invite</a> Nashville police to assist in providing security for First Lady Michelle Obama&#8217;s visit to the Music City. It is not known whether the dispute over the warrant factored into that decision, but it is unprecedented for local police to be left out of security plans during a visit by a first lady.</p> <div class="mr_social_sharing_wrapper">  <span class="mr_social_sharing"><fb:share-button type="button_count" href="http://benswann.com/oath-upheld-nashville-cops-refused-secret-service-request-for-illegal-search-of-obama-critic/"></fb:share-button></span><span class="mr_social_sharing"><div class="g-plusone"          form.onsubmit = function(event) {     validate();     if(!isValid) {       revalidateOnChange();       return false;     }   };      function validate() {     isValid = true;     emailValidation();     fieldsValidation();     listsValidation();     updateFormAfterValidation();   }    function emailValidation() {     var email = document.getElementById("signup_email");     if(!validEmail.test(email.value)) {       errorMessage(email);       isValid = false;     } else {       removeErrorMessage(email);     }   }    function fieldsValidation() {     for(var i = 0; i < form.elements.length; ++i) {       var input = form.elements[i];       if(input.id == "signup_email") continue;       if(input.className.indexOf("required") >= 0) {         if(input.value == "") {           errorMessage(input)           isValid = false;         } else {           removeErrorMessage(input);         isValid = false;       } else {         mainListsDiv.className = mainListsDiv.className.replace(/ invalid/g, "");       }     }   }    function errorMessage(input) {     input.className   = "required invalid"; "submit" : "disabled";   }    function submitButtonText() {     var text;     if(isValid) {       text = submit.getAttribute("data-default-text");     } else {       var allFieldsValid = return text;   }    function checkIfAllFieldsAreValid() {     var allFieldsValid = true     for(var i = 0; i < form.elements.length; ++i) {       var input = form.elements[i];       if(input.placeholder && input.placeholder.length > 0) allFieldsValid = false;     }     return allFieldsValid;   }    function revalidateOnChange() {     for(var i = 0; i < form.elements.length; ++i) McCullar</span> </cite> </div> <div id="dsq-comment-body-90816" class="dsq-comment-body"> <div id="dsq-comment-message-90816" class="dsq-comment-message"><p>Title 18, U.S.C., Section 242<br/> Deprivation of Rights Under Color of Law</p> <p>This statute makes it a crime for any<br/> person acting under color of law, statute, ordinance, regulation, or<br/> custom to willfully deprive or cause to be deprived from any person<br/> those rights, privileges, or immunities secured or protected by the<br/> Constitution and laws of the U.S.</p> <p>This law further prohibits a person acting<br/> under color of law, statute, ordinance, regulation or custom to<br/> willfully subject or cause to be subjected any person to different<br/> punishments, pains, or penalties, than those prescribed for punishment<br/> of citizens on account of such person being an alien or by reason of<br/> his/her color or race.</p> <p>Acts under &#8220;color of any law&#8221; include acts<br/> not only done by federal, state, or local officials within the bounds<br/> or limits of their lawful authority, but also acts done without and<br/> beyond the bounds of their lawful authority; provided that, in order for<br/> unlawful acts of any official to be done under &#8220;color of any law,&#8221; the<br/> unlawful acts must be done while such official is purporting or<br/> pretending to act in the performance of his/her official duties. This<br/> definition includes, in addition to law enforcement officials,<br/> individuals such as Mayors, Council persons, Judges, Nursing Home<br/> Proprietors, Security Guards, etc., persons who are bound by laws,<br/> statutes ordinances, or customs.</p> <p>Punishment varies from a fine or<br/> imprisonment of up to one year, or both, and if bodily injury results or<br/> if such acts include the use, attempted use, or threatened use of a<br/> dangerous weapon, explosives, or fire shall be fined or imprisoned up to<br/> ten years or both, and if death results, or if such acts include<br/> kidnapping or an attempt to kidnap, aggravated sexual abuse or an<br/> attempt to commit aggravated sexual abuse, or an attempt to kill, shall<br/> be fined under this title, or imprisoned for any term of years or for<br/> life, or both, or may be sentenced to death.</p> </div> </div> </li>  <li class="comment odd alt depth-3" id="dsq-comment-90821"> <div id="dsq-comment-header-90821" class="dsq-comment-header"> <cite id="dsq-cite-90821"> <span id="dsq-author-user-90821">Jake Davidson</span> </cite> </div> <div id="dsq-comment-body-90821" class="dsq-comment-body"> <div id="dsq-comment-message-90821" class="dsq-comment-message"><p>Um so a state actor will arrest a federal agent under federal law?</p> </div> </div> </li>  </ul>  </li>  </ul>  </li>  <li class="comment even thread-odd thread-alt depth-1" id="dsq-comment-90720"> <div id="dsq-comment-header-90720" class="dsq-comment-header"> <cite id="dsq-cite-90720"> <span id="dsq-author-user-90720">Robbie Cheney</span> </cite> </div> <div id="dsq-comment-body-90720" class="dsq-comment-body"> <div id="dsq-comment-message-90720" class="dsq-comment-message"><p>Glad to see the Nashville PD stand up for a citizen. For exact details read the Metropolitan Nashville-Davidson County charter.</p> <p>I think this is common to most places that have combined city and county governments.</p> </div> </div> <ul class="children"> <li class="comment odd alt depth-5" id="dsq-comment-92087"> <div id="dsq-comment-header-92087" class="dsq-comment-header"> <cite id="dsq-cite-92087"> <span id="dsq-author-user-92087">madmemere</span> </cite> </div> <div id="dsq-comment-body-92087" class="dsq-comment-body"> <div id="dsq-comment-message-92087" class="dsq-comment-message"><p>Thanks for the info.</p> </div> </div> </li>  <li class="comment even depth-5" id="dsq-comment-92241"> <div id="dsq-comment-header-92241" class="dsq-comment-header"> <cite id="dsq-cite-92241"> http://www.robbiestewart.ga <span id="dsq-author-user-92241">Robbie</span> </cite> </div> <div id="dsq-comment-body-92241" class="dsq-comment-body"> <div id="dsq-comment-message-92241" class="dsq-comment-message"><p>1980&#8242;s?? I think you meant the 1960&#8242;s dude. The Metropolitan Charter that consolidated both Nashville and Davidson County into one government came into effect in 1962. The reason why voters chose to do this was because many business at the time were moving out of Nashville&#8217;s city limits to avoid the higher taxes and as a result, many of the suburban areas were growing to the point of where the Davidson County Sheriff&#8217;s Department could no longer provide effective police protection in those areas, so in the elections of 1960, the residents of both the city and county both voted in favor of a Metropolitan form of government. Two of the stipulations in the Metropolitan Charter were that residents in the old Nashville city limits would be taxed at an urban services district rate while those in the suburban areas would be taxed at a lessor rate and also the cities of Goodlettsville, Bellevue, and Belle Meade would continue to retain their independent city status including taxation and maintaining their own police departments. While the Tennessee Constitution does designate that the sheriff is the chief law enforcement officer of the county, it does make an exception for counties that are governed by a metropolitan or county charter as Davidson County is, so that&#8217;s why the sheriff there has limited power to being the officer of the courts, jail, and serving warrants. Another county in Tennessee, Knox County has tried many times to consolidate both the City of Knoxville and Knox County governments into one government, however, in every election that was held, residents in the city would vote in favor of it while residents in the county would vote against it. Knox County government is, however, governed by a county charter that has certain stipulations in it including term limits for elected officials including the county mayor, sheriff, etc, while most other counties in Tennessee do not.</p> </div> </div> </li>  </ul>  </li>  <li class="comment odd alt depth-4" id="dsq-comment-102193"> <div id="dsq-comment-header-102193" class="dsq-comment-header"> <cite id="dsq-cite-102193"> <span id="dsq-author-user-102193">localhost</span> </cite> </div> <div id="dsq-comment-body-102193" class="dsq-comment-body"> <div id="dsq-comment-message-102193" class="dsq-comment-message"><p>I can&#8217;t speak for other states, but in CT a sheriff&#8217;s duties are limited to serving divorce papers and escorting prisoners.
